533:**New values added:**
534:
535:- `'retrieval.embedding_failed'` — emitted when the query embedding throws or times out.
536:- `'retrieval.empty_after_semantic'` — emitted when semantic filtering reduces a non-empty pool to zero for a category and the legacy fallback is applied.
537:
538:**Producer:** `retrievalService.assembleKnowledgeForRun` (two emission sites).
539:
540:**Consumer:** `retrievalObservabilityService` (which surfaces degraded reasons on the run trace).
541:
542:---
543:
544:## 7. Permissions / RLS checklist
545:
546:### 7.1 `memory_block_version_sources` (new tenant-scoped table — Phase 1)
547:
548:| Requirement | Status |
549:|-------------|--------|
550:| RLS policy in the same migration | ✓ migration `0330` |
551:| `RLS_PROTECTED_TABLES` manifest entry | ✓ |
552:| Route guard | ✓ `GET /api/memory-blocks/:id/sources` behind `authenticate` + `requirePermission('memory_block.view')` or equivalent (build phase pins the exact permission key; the existing memory-block detail routes are the reference) |
553:| Principal-scoped context | n/a — admin/operator route only, not an agent execution path |
554:
555:The policy uses the canonical three-layer pattern: `current_setting('app.organisation_id', true)::uuid`. `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` applied for defence-in-depth.
556:
557:### 7.2 `agent_runs.injected_entry_ids` (new column — Phase 2)
558:
559:| Requirement | Status |
560:|-------------|--------|
561:| RLS posture | inherited from `agent_runs` (already RLS-protected; column addition does not change posture) |
562:| Manifest entry | n/a — column, not table |
563:| Route guard | n/a — column read via existing run-detail routes (which are already guarded) |
564:| Principal-scoped context | inherited |
565:
566:### 7.3 `mv_memory_utility_30d` (new materialised view — Phase 2)
567:
568:| Requirement | Status |
569:|-------------|--------|
570:| RLS posture | **Materialised views do not enforce RLS by themselves.** The read service `memoryUtilityQueryService.ts` MUST filter rows by `current_setting('app.organisation_id')` in the WHERE clause, or call the view via `withAdminConnection` only from server-side aggregations that are not user-facing. The B2 admin route filters by org before returning. |
571:| Manifest entry | The view is added to a new `RLS_EXCLUDED_VIEWS` registry if one exists; if not, the convention is `rlsExclusions` in `server/middleware/orgScoping.ts` (per `mv_optimiser_peer_medians` precedent — migration 0277). |
572:| Route guard | ✓ `GET /api/usage/memory-utility` behind `authenticate` + admin permission (build phase pins the key; existing usage routes are the reference). |
573:| Refresh-job posture | The refresh job runs in `withAdminConnection` (multi-tenant refresh in a single transaction). |
574:
575:### 7.4 Cross-tenant leak class — explicit risks and mitigations
576:
577:- **Lineage row exposure across organisations.** `memory_block_version_sources.organisation_id` is the RLS predicate. Migrations verify `FORCE RLS`. The route resolves `organisation_id` from the authenticated user's session, not from path params, before joining.
578:- **Materialised view cross-tenant rows.** The view aggregates per `(organisation_id, subaccount_id, agent_id)`. The read query filters by the session's `organisation_id`. The view itself is not RLS-protected — protection is at the read service.
579:- **Injected entry IDs across organisations.** `injected_entry_ids` is a column on `agent_runs`, which is already RLS-protected. No new exposure.
580:
581:---
582:
583:## 8. Execution model
584:
585:### 8.1 Phase-by-phase model
586:
587:| Phase | Operation | Model | Justification |
588:|-------|-----------|-------|---------------|
589:| 1 | Lineage row insert at synthesis | Inline / synchronous, inside the same transaction as block-version insert | Cluster array is in scope at the call site; atomicity (block version + lineage rows commit together) is a correctness requirement, not a performance optimisation |
590:| 1 | `GET /api/memory-blocks/:id/sources` | Inline / synchronous request | Standard admin route; no batch processing |
591:| 2 | `injected_entry_ids` write | Inline / synchronous, alongside other `agent_runs` writes at run-end / memory-injection time | Already part of the existing run-state write path; adding a column write is not a new transactional boundary |
592:| 2 | Materialised-view refresh | Queued / asynchronous (pg-boss) — nightly at 03:00 UTC | View must refresh during low-traffic; `REFRESH CONCURRENTLY` requires the view to have a unique index (provided in migration) |
593:| 3 | Query embedding + cosine score | Inline / synchronous, per agent run | Result must be available before retrieval result is returned to the caller (`agentExecutionService.ts:921-922`) |
594:| 3 | Degraded-reason event emission | Inline / synchronous, via existing observability service | Mirrors existing degraded-reason emission |
595:| 4 | `GET /api/usage/memory-utility` | Inline / synchronous request | Standard usage route |
596:
597:### 8.2 Cache-boundary impact
598:
599:- Phase 1 lineage inserts and Phase 2 manifest writes do not change the prompt content or the assembly pipeline → no cache boundary impact.
600:- Phase 3 changes the **selection** of retrieved chunks/blocks but not the rendered shape, so the existing `stablePrefix` / `dynamicSuffix` boundaries at `agentExecutionService.ts:1254-1257` are unaffected. The agent prompt format is unchanged.
601:- D's selection change does cache-invalidate the `dynamicSuffix` partition when the retrieved set differs run-to-run, which it already does today (recency-ordered). No regression.
602:
603:### 8.3 Latency budget
604:
605:- Query embedding adds one OpenAI call per run (when flag is on). Brief estimates ~$0.00002 per call (`text-embedding-3-small`) and ~50–150ms RTT. The brief flags this as negligible cost; latency impact is bounded by the existing run-orchestration timeout envelope.
606:- Materialised-view refresh runs out-of-band (nightly cron), no inline impact.
607:
608:---
609:

/**
 * Tables explicitly excluded from RLS enforcement.
 *
 * Every table in the application database should either:
 *   1. Appear in `RLS_PROTECTED_TABLES` (server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts)
 *      with a matching `CREATE POLICY` in a migration, or
 *   2. Appear here with a documented rationale explaining why RLS is not
 *      applicable (platform-level data, cross-org data, etc.).
 *
 * The CI gate `scripts/gates/verify-rls-coverage.sh` checks that every
 * table is accounted for in one of these two lists.
 */

export interface RlsExclusion {
  tableName: string;
  rationale: string;
}

export const RLS_EXCLUSIONS: ReadonlyArray<RlsExclusion> = [
  { tableName: 'organisations', rationale: 'Platform-level ƒ?" no tenant column' },
  { tableName: 'users', rationale: 'Cross-org ƒ?" users can belong to multiple orgs' },
  { tableName: 'system_agents', rationale: 'Platform templates ƒ?" identical for all orgs' },
  { tableName: 'skill_definitions', rationale: 'System-managed skill catalogue' },
  { tableName: 'optimiser_skill_peer_medians', rationale: 'Cross-tenant aggregate p50/p95/p99 per skill_slug; no per-tenant rows in projection; HAVING n_tenants >= 5; admin_role only via REVOKE/GRANT' },
];

export const RLS_EXCLUDED_TABLE_NAMES: ReadonlySet<string> = new Set(
  RLS_EXCLUSIONS.map((t) => t.tableName),
);

codex
1. **Lines 291-304, 337-339, 356-357, 503**  
   **Type:** contradiction  
   Phase 4 is labeled “UI only,” but the phase also adds a new server route and a new server query service.  
   **Minimum fix:** remove “UI only,” or move the route/query work into explicit Phase 4 backend scope.

2. **Lines 201-246, 295-297, 497-509**  
   **Type:** missing mechanism / contradiction  
   B2 requires two 30-day rolling line charts, but `mv_memory_utility_30d` only returns one aggregate row per `(organisation_id, subaccount_id, agent_id)`. There is no date bucket, no daily series, and no per-run row in the view output despite the prose claiming “per-run raw counts.”  
   **Minimum fix:** either define a date-bucketed view/contract that can drive line charts, or change the UI spec to aggregate cards/table only.

3. **Lines 300, 572, 782**  
   **Type:** under-specified route / existing-primitive drift  
   The spec proposes `GET /api/usage/memory-utility?organisation_id=X` and says existing usage routes follow that pattern, but the current usage surface is path-scoped (`/api/orgs/:orgId/usage/*`, `/api/subaccounts/:subaccountId/usage/*`) and `UsagePage` is subaccount-scoped.  
   **Minimum fix:** lock one concrete route family and scope now: org-scoped or subaccount-scoped.

4. **Lines 349, 352, 357**  
   **Type:** file-inventory drift  
   `server/routes/index.ts` and `server/jobs/index.ts` are listed as modified files, but those files do not exist in the repo; route/job registration currently happens in `server/index.ts`.  
   **Minimum fix:** replace those entries with `server/index.ts`.

5. **Lines 338-339, 361-372, 566-573**  
   **Type:** file-inventory drift  
   §7.3 says the materialized view must be added to an exclusion registry, but §5 does not inventory the file that would be edited for that.  
   **Minimum fix:** add the actual exclusion-registry file to §5.

6. **Lines 570-571**  
   **Type:** file/name drift  
   The spec references a possible `RLS_EXCLUDED_VIEWS` registry or `server/middleware/orgScoping.ts`, but the repo already has `server/db/rlsExclusions.ts` / `RLS_EXCLUSIONS`.  
   **Minimum fix:** name the exact existing registry/file and use that consistently throughout the spec.

7. **Lines 150-187, 546-555**  
   **Type:** missing mechanism / permissions ambiguity  
   Phase 1 creates a new RLS-forced tenant table and writes to it, but the migration only defines a `USING` policy. There is no concrete INSERT/`WITH CHECK` policy, and no explicit statement that writes use a privileged connection.  
   **Minimum fix:** add the concrete INSERT policy or explicitly state the privileged write posture.

8. **Lines 89, 103, 162, 171**  
   **Type:** schema ambiguity  
   `source_entry_id_hash` and `source_run_id_hash` are load-bearing deletion-safe columns, but their algorithm is unspecified. `content_hash` is concrete (`SHA-256`); these are only “hex digest, deterministic from UUID.”  
   **Minimum fix:** specify the exact algorithm and encoding.

9. **Lines 100-106, 169-172, 473**  
   **Type:** load-bearing claim without contract  
   The spec says lineage rows must capture `source_run_id_hash` and `source_run_label_at_capture` when a run is available, but both columns are nullable and no DB or write-path rule enforces population when `source_run_id` is present.  
   **Minimum fix:** add a CHECK or explicit write invariant tying those fields to non-null `source_run_id`.

10. **Lines 87-94, 166, 189**  
    **Type:** load-bearing claim without contract  
    `quality_score_at_capture` is listed as required deletion-safe metadata, and the write site says per-entry quality is already in scope, but the schema still leaves the column nullable with no allowed-null rule.  
    **Minimum fix:** make it non-null or specify exactly when null is legal.

11. **Lines 260-262, 807-808**  
    **Type:** under-specified load-bearing decision  
    Phase 3 leaves both the semantic query definition and the threshold default open to build-phase judgment. Those choices change retrieval behavior materially.  
    **Minimum fix:** lock the exact query source and exact default threshold in the spec.

12. **Lines 250, 479-495, 718-723, 809**  
    **Type:** under-specified write contract  
    `InjectedEntryManifest` says prompt content is the canonical source of truth, but the exact write site is still left for build phase to find.  
    **Minimum fix:** pin the exact function block / statement where `injected_entry_ids` is written.

13. **Lines 250, 591, 720-723**  
    **Type:** contradiction  
    The Phase 2 write timing is inconsistent. §4 says write immediately after prompt-inclusion filtering; §8 says “run-end / memory-injection time.”  
    **Minimum fix:** choose one timing and transaction boundary and use it everywhere.

14. **Lines 193, 438-442, 646, 774**  
    **Type:** contradiction  
    The bidirectional lineage expander is described as optional/deferred, but §14.1 specifies it as present in the v1 component, collapsed by default.  
    **Minimum fix:** either make it in-scope and remove the deferral, or remove it from the v1 UI contract.

15. **Lines 40, 197-254, 291-304, 622, 664**  
    **Type:** contradiction  
    §11 says each goal maps to exactly one phase, but Proposal B is explicitly split across Phase 2 and Phase 4. §9.1 also says `injected_entry_ids` is referenced only by Phase 4’s view aggregation, even though Phase 2 defines that view.  
    **Minimum fix:** rewrite §9.1 and §11 to match the actual phase split.

16. **Lines 174-175, 707-711**  
    **Type:** missing mechanism / execution-safety gap  
    The idempotency contract for lineage inserts assumes retries “insert no new rows,” but a unique constraint alone will still abort the transaction unless the insert uses `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` or equivalent.  
    **Minimum fix:** specify the exact conflict-handling SQL.

17. **Lines 739-740**  
    **Type:** contradiction  
    The Phase 3 terminal-event contract says the run emits “exactly one of” `retrieval.embedding_failed`, `retrieval.empty_after_semantic`, or none, then says those states are not mutually exclusive.  
    **Minimum fix:** state the real allowed combinations explicitly.

18. **Lines 552, 810**  
    **Type:** under-specified permission / existing-primitive drift  
    The Sources route permission is still open, and the placeholder `memory_block.view` does not match the existing memory-block route primitive, which uses `requireOrgPermission(ORG_PERMISSIONS.AGENTS_VIEW)`.  
    **Minimum fix:** name the exact permission constant in the spec.

19. **Lines 369-370**  
    **Type:** file-inventory drift  
    `docs/spec-context.md` appears in the file inventory while the row says “No update needed,” then conditionally suggests a future change. A file lock cannot include conditional/non-touch entries.  
    **Minimum fix:** remove it from §5 or make the change concrete and mandatory.

20. **Lines 91, 161, 189, 413**  
    **Type:** under-specified type  
    The Phase 1 mechanism only writes lineage from `WorkspaceMemoryEntry[]` and stores `source_entry_id` as an FK to `workspace_memory_entries`, but the payload/schema advertise `agent_belief` and `correction` source types with no concrete writer or storage model for them.  
    **Minimum fix:** narrow v1 to `workspace_memory`, or define the concrete polymorphic source mechanism.

21. **Lines 570-573, 577-579**  
    **Type:** permissions ambiguity  
    The materialized-view protection story is not fully concrete: the spec says the read service “MUST filter by `current_setting('app.organisation_id')` in the WHERE clause, or call via `withAdminConnection` only from server-side aggregations that are not user-facing,” but B2 is user-facing and no exact query contract is pinned.  
    **Minimum fix:** specify the exact read posture for the B2 route, including whether it uses org-scoped DB access or `withAdminConnection` plus explicit `organisation_id = req.orgId` filtering.
